<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="vertical-align:middle; font-size:95%;"><b>This article contains <a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">Korean</a> text.</b> Without proper <a href="/wiki/Help:Multilingual_support_(East_Asian)" title="Help:Multilingual support (East Asian)">rendering support</a>, you may see <a href="/wiki/Specials_(Unicode_block)#Replacement_character" title="Specials (Unicode block)">question marks, boxes, or other symbols</a> instead of <a href="/wiki/Hangul" title="Hangul">Hangul</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hanja" title="Hanja">Hanja</a>.</td>

<p><b>Jung Ji-hoon</b> (<a href="/wiki/Hangul" title="Hangul">Hangul</a>: <span lang="ko-Hang">정지훈</span>; <a href="/wiki/Hanja" title="Hanja">Hanja</a>: <span lang="ko-Hani">鄭智薰</span>, born June 25, 1982), better known by his <a href="/wiki/Stage_name" title="Stage name">stage name</a> <b>Rain</b> (Korean 비 IPA ['piː]), is a <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korean</a> singer-songwriter, actor, and music producer.</p>
<p>Rain's musical career includes seven albums (six Korean, one Japanese), 28 singles and numerous concert tours around the world. He first achieved breakthrough success with his third Korean album, <i><a href="/wiki/It%27s_Raining_(album)" title="It's Raining (album)">It's Raining</a></i> (2004), which spawned the <a href="/wiki/It%27s_Raining_(Rain_song)" title="It's Raining (Rain song)">number one single of the same name</a>. The album sold a million copies in Asia, and established Rain as an international star.</p>
<p>Rain made his acting debut in the 2003 drama <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sang_Doo!_Let%27s_Go_To_School" title="Sang Doo! Let's Go To School">Sang Doo! Let's Go To School</a></i>. His lead role in the pan-Asia hit drama <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Full_House_(2004_TV_series)" title="Full House (2004 TV series)">Full House</a></i> (2004) established his status as a Hallyu star. In 2008, Rain made his Hollywood debut in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Speed_Racer_(film)" title="Speed Racer (film)">Speed Racer</a></i> and starred in <i><a href="/wiki/Ninja_Assassin" title="Ninja Assassin">Ninja Assassin</a></i> (2009), the latter of which made him the first Korean to win an <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, Rain set up his own company, R.A.I.N. Company.</p>
<p></p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Acting_career"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Acting career</span></a>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Rain lost his mother as she struggled with diabetes and died in December 2000. Within that same year, Rain was recruited as a trainee for <a href="/wiki/JYP_Entertainment" title="JYP Entertainment">JYP Entertainment</a>, led by recording artist and producer <a href="/wiki/Park_Jin-young" title="Park Jin-young">Park Jin-young</a>. In a CNN interview and also in a Discovery Channel documentary called <i>Discovering Hip Korea</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> he recalled being repeatedly rejected because of his looks: "In fact, I was told after one audition that my singing and dancing was great but I did not make it because I did not have <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_blepharoplasty" title="Asian blepharoplasty">double eyelids</a>." However, he finally got in as producer <a href="/wiki/Park_Jin-young" title="Park Jin-young">Park Jin-young</a> saw his drive and persistence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (December 2011)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> During the early years of training, Rain was a backup dancer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-multiple_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-multiple-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Singing_career">Singing career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Singing career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="1998–2000:_Debut_in_boy_band_Fanclub"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1998.E2.80.932000:_Debut_in_boy_band_Fanclub">1998–2000: Debut in boy band Fanclub</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1998–2000: Debut in boy band Fanclub">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Jung Ji-hoon was 16 years old when he debuted as a member of a boy band called Fanclub (팬클럽).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boyband_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-boyband-2">[2]</a></sup> The band did not garner much attention, though they released two albums.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="2002–06:_Debut_as_solo_singer_and_Pan-Asia_success"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2002.E2.80.9306:_Debut_as_solo_singer_and_Pan-Asia_success">2002–06: Debut as solo singer and Pan-Asia success</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2002–06: Debut as solo singer and Pan-Asia success">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2002, Jung debuted as a solo singer with his first solo album titled <i><a href="/wiki/Bad_Guy_(album)" title="Bad Guy (album)">Bad Guy</a></i> where he was introduced to the media through his stage name, Rain. Two singles were released from the album - the eponymous title track "Bad Guy" and "Handshake". Following the success of his debut, Rain released his second album, <i><a href="/wiki/Rain_2" title="Rain 2">Rain 2</a></i> with the lead single "<a href="/wiki/Ways_to_Avoid_the_Sun" title="Ways to Avoid the Sun">Ways to Avoid the Sun</a>". From 2003-2004, he became a host for <a href="/wiki/Korean_Broadcasting_System" title="Korean Broadcasting System">KBS</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Music_Bank_(TV_series)" title="Music Bank (TV series)">Music Bank</a></i>.</p>
<p>Rain then released his third album, <i><a href="/wiki/It%27s_Raining_(album)" title="It's Raining (album)">It's Raining</a></i>, which topped music charts in Korea as well as throughout Asia. To promote the release, Rain then embarked on his first concert, <i><a href="/wiki/Rainy_Day_2005_Tour" title="Rainy Day 2005 Tour">Rainy Day 2005 Tour</a></i>, which spanned a total of 14 concerts in 8 countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The album went on to sell over a million copies in Asia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> cementing Rain's position as one of the region's top musical acts.</p>
<h3><span id="2006–07:_Expansion_outside_Korea"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2006.E2.80.9307:_Expansion_outside_Korea">2006–07: Expansion outside Korea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2006–07: Expansion outside Korea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:207px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bi_(Rain).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2046" data-file-width="1566" height="268" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Bi_%28Rain%29.jpg/205px-Bi_%28Rain%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Bi_%28Rain%29.jpg/308px-Bi_%28Rain%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Bi_%28Rain%29.jpg/410px-Bi_%28Rain%29.jpg 2x" width="205"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bi_(Rain).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rain during a performance.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:203px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rain_Korean_Singer.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="480" height="268" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Rain_Korean_Singer.JPG/201px-Rain_Korean_Singer.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Rain_Korean_Singer.JPG/301px-Rain_Korean_Singer.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Rain_Korean_Singer.JPG/402px-Rain_Korean_Singer.JPG 2x" width="201"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rain_Korean_Singer.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rain in Bangkok 2007</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Rain released his first Japanese album, <i><a href="/wiki/Eternal_Rain" title="Eternal Rain">Eternal Rain</a></i> on September 13, 2006. He held his first Japanese solo concert, <i>Rainy Day Japan</i>. Tickets to the concert were sold out 30 seconds after going on sale at the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_International_Forum" title="Tokyo International Forum">Tokyo International Forum</a>. This was followed up by the release of his fourth album, <i><a href="/wiki/Rain%27s_World" title="Rain's World">Rain's World</a></i>, which also sold over a million copies in Asia and further established him as one of the top musical acts in Southeast Asia. The success of the album lead to a repackage album, which was released 2 months later.</p>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Rain%27s_Coming_World_Tour" title="Rain's Coming World Tour">Rain's Coming World Tour</a></i> began on December 15, 2006 at <a href="/wiki/Seoul_Olympic_Stadium" title="Seoul Olympic Stadium">Seoul Olympic Stadium</a> in Seoul and was scheduled to continue through 2007 to various parts of Asia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> His tour incorporated the talents of producers and stage designers (such as Jamie King and Roy Bennett) who have been involved with the concert tours of other artists such as <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Martin" title="Ricky Martin">Ricky Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">The Rolling Stones</a>. Ticket sales were expected to be over <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>100 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>On May 25, 2007, Rain became the first Korean star to perform at the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Dome" title="Tokyo Dome">Tokyo Dome</a>. The concert attracted nearly 55,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2007, Rain left the management of <a href="/wiki/JYP_Entertainment" title="JYP Entertainment">JYP Entertainment</a> to start his own company, <a href="/wiki/J._Tune_Entertainment" title="J. Tune Entertainment">J. Tune Entertainment</a>, but still retains collaborative relationship with <a href="/wiki/Park_Jin-young" title="Park Jin-young">Park Jin-young</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In April 2006, Rain was mentioned by <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> magazine which listed him as one of the "100 Most Influential People Who Shape Our World."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Time-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> In 2007, Rain topped <i>Time</i> Magazine's online user poll, defeating <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Colbert" title="Stephen Colbert">Stephen Colbert</a> by 100,000 votes;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Colbert jokingly retaliated by producing a parody of Rain's music video for "Ways to Avoid the Sun" called "He's Singin' In Korean", and challenged Rain to a dance-off or a "cuddle-off", or a "spoon-off". On May 5, 2008, Rain appeared in a surprise guest segment at the end of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Colbert_Report" title="The Colbert Report">The Colbert Report</a></i>, and proceeded to engage Colbert in a dance-off on a <a href="/wiki/Dance_Dance_Revolution" title="Dance Dance Revolution">Dance Dance Revolution</a> machine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Episode_.2304060_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Episode_.2304060-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> He also made it into <i><a href="/wiki/People_(magazine)" title="People (magazine)">People's</a></i> 2007 list of the "Most Beautiful People" in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> In a press release, Rain stated that he was honored to be on the list, and also noted that it will be a great boost to his efforts to raise his public awareness in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yahoo_Canada_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo_Canada-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rain's concerts in the United States were also well received. His two-day concert, <i><a href="/wiki/Rainy_Day_2005_Tour" title="Rainy Day 2005 Tour">Rainy Day New York</a></i>, held at the <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a>, were sold out within a matter of days. The concert was marketed and promoted by the Asian concert production company Rainstone Live.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Rain also performed two concert dates in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Vegas,_Nevada" title="Las Vegas, Nevada">Las Vegas, Nevada</a> on December 23–24, 2006; held at <a href="/wiki/The_Colosseum_at_Caesars_Palace" title="The Colosseum at Caesars Palace">The Colosseum at Caesars Palace</a>.</p>
<h3><span id="2008–12:_Rainism,_Back_to_the_Basic_and_continued_popularity"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2008.E2.80.9312:_Rainism.2C_Back_to_the_Basic_and_continued_popularity">2008–12: <i>Rainism, Back to the Basic</i> and continued popularity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2008–12: Rainism, Back to the Basic and continued popularity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:203px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RainF1.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="268" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/RainF1.JPG/201px-RainF1.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/RainF1.JPG/301px-RainF1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/RainF1.JPG/402px-RainF1.JPG 2x" width="201"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RainF1.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rain at Sepang International Circuit F1 2011 post-party concert, Malaysia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On October 16, 2008, Rain released his fifth Korean album, <i><a href="/wiki/Rainism" title="Rainism">Rainism</a></i>, which spawned the number one hit single "Love Story". The music video for "Love Story" featured Korean actress <a href="/wiki/Ha_Ji-won" title="Ha Ji-won">Ha Ji-won</a>. A second single, titled "Rainisim", was subsequently released. On November 24, 2008, the Commission of Youth Protection deemed the album inappropriate for people under 19 years old because the lyrics in the song "Rainism" were considered problematic due to their phallic and sexual references.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Rain re-released a "clean version" of "Rainism" shortly after, but instead of changing the original album's contents, he labeled a sticker that deemed "Rainism" inappropriate for those under 19 years old.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In October 2009, in support of his fifth album <i>Rainism</i>, Rain kicked off his Asian tour, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Legend_of_Rainism_Asia_Tour" title="The Legend of Rainism Asia Tour">The Legend of Rainism Tour</a></i> with two shows at <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Gymnastics_Arena" title="Olympic Gymnastics Arena">Olympic Gymnastics Arena</a> in Seoul on October 9 and 10.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> It continued with concerts in various parts of Asia and concluded at <a href="/wiki/The_Colosseum_at_Caesars_Palace" title="The Colosseum at Caesars Palace">The Colosseum at Caesars Palace</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Vegas,_Nevada" title="Las Vegas, Nevada">Las Vegas, Nevada</a>, on December 24–25, 2009.</p>
<p>On April 6, 2010, Rain released a special mini-album titled <i><a href="/wiki/Back_to_the_Basic" title="Back to the Basic">Back to the Basic</a></i>, including the singles "Love Song" starring <a href="/wiki/Han_Ye-seul" title="Han Ye-seul">Han Ye-seul</a> in the music video as well as "Hip Song". Once again, Rain topped <i>Time</i> Magazine's TIME 100 poll.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> In October, Rain represented Korea and performed at the <a href="/wiki/Asia_Song_Festival" title="Asia Song Festival">7th Asia Song Festival</a>, organised by Korea Foundation for International Culture Exchange, at the <a href="/wiki/Seoul_Olympic_Stadium" title="Seoul Olympic Stadium">Seoul Olympic Stadium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>The following year, Rain made his third appearance in the TIME 100 poll. <i>Time</i> describes his win as "The South Korean pop star turned actor Rain, 28, took the top spot in the TIME 100 reader poll for the third year, trouncing competitors from Barack Obama to Lady Gaga. That's pretty impressive online power for a guy whose main claim to Western fame is a role in the 2009 film Ninja Assassin."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>Along with the TIME honor, Rain went on a farewell tour, The Best Show Tour, before his 21-month compulsory military service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The tour spanned Southeast Asia including his first tour dates throughout South Korea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="2013–2014:_CUBE_Entertainment_and_Rain_Effect"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2013.E2.80.932014:_CUBE_Entertainment_and_Rain_Effect">2013–2014: CUBE Entertainment and <i>Rain Effect</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2013–2014: CUBE Entertainment and Rain Effect">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rain_US_military_concert.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Rain_US_military_concert.JPG/220px-Rain_US_military_concert.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Rain_US_military_concert.JPG/330px-Rain_US_military_concert.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Rain_US_military_concert.JPG/440px-Rain_US_military_concert.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rain_US_military_concert.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rain performs at a K-pop concert at <a href="/wiki/Kunsan_Air_Base" title="Kunsan Air Base">Kunsan Air Base</a> in September 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On September 17, it was officially announced that Rain signed with <a href="/wiki/Cube_Entertainment#Cube_DC" title="Cube Entertainment">Cube DC</a>, a sub-label of Cube Entertainment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> After signing with Cube DC, it was announced Rain would be going on his first tour since his discharge. The <i>2013 Zepp Tour: Story of Rain</i> saw Rain perform 10 dates in four cities in <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> over a few dates in November.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>His first official public appearance since leaving the military occurred during <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mode_Creation_Munich" title="Mode Creation Munich">MCM</a>'s store opening in <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> at The Shoppes at <a href="/wiki/Marina_Bay_Sands" title="Marina Bay Sands">Marina Bay Sands</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> followed by the BAZAAR Men Style People of The Year Award Ceremony in <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> In October, Rain held his first fan meeting since his discharge in <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a>. While on tour, Rain delivered a special performance at the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Mnet_Asian_Music_Awards" title="Mnet Asian Music Awards">MAMA</a>, where a trailer teasing an upcoming reality show and new album was revealed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>As a precursor to his new album, Rain starred in a reality show <i>Rain Effect</i>, which premiered on December 19.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The new album, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Rain_Effect" title="Rain Effect">Rain Effect</a></i>, was released on January 2, 2014 with music videos for double title tracks, "30 Sexy" and "La Song".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="2015–present:_R.A.I.N._Company,_The_Squall_Tour_and_Upcoming_Album"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2015.E2.80.93present:_R.A.I.N._Company.2C_The_Squall_Tour_and_Upcoming_Album">2015–present: R.A.I.N. Company, The Squall Tour and Upcoming Album</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2015–present: R.A.I.N. Company, The Squall Tour and Upcoming Album">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On September 7, 2015, Rain announced through his Facebook page that he and the CEO came to a mutual decision to not renew his contract with <a href="/wiki/Cube_Entertainment" title="Cube Entertainment">Cube Entertainment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allkpop.com_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-allkpop.com-40">[40]</a></sup> After parting ways with Cube,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-41">[41]</a></sup> on October 11, 2015, he announced through his official website that he had created his own one-man agency with the aid of his longtime manager and other entertainment figures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Korean_Times_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Korean_Times-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rain announced that he would be embarking on another world tour. The tour, titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Squall_World_Tour" title="The Squall World Tour">The Squall</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> starts from <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, with the potential to expand into Japan, Europe and America.</p>
<p>On December 12, 2016, RAIN Company announced that Rain would release a new album in 2017 with a series of promotional activities to accompany his musical comeback.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>On January 14, 2017, Rain made his comeback with the single "The Best Present", produced by <a href="/wiki/Psy" title="Psy">Psy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Acting_career">Acting career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Acting career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="2003–2006:_Acting_debut_and_Hallyu_fame"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2003.E2.80.932006:_Acting_debut_and_Hallyu_fame">2003–2006: Acting debut and Hallyu fame</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 2003–2006: Acting debut and Hallyu fame">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Rain made his television debut in the <a href="/wiki/Korean_Broadcasting_System" title="Korean Broadcasting System">KBS</a> drama, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sang_Doo!_Let%27s_Go_To_School" title="Sang Doo! Let's Go To School">Sang Doo! Let's Go To School</a></i> (2003). The drama achieved good ratings and he won the Most Popular TV Actor award at the 2004 <a href="/wiki/Baeksang_Arts_Awards" title="Baeksang Arts Awards">Baeksang Arts Awards</a>.</p>
<p>In 2004, Rain's popularity continued to climb when starred alongside <a href="/wiki/Song_Hye-kyo" title="Song Hye-kyo">Song Hye-kyo</a> in the hit romantic comedy series <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Full_House_(Korean_drama)" title="Full House (Korean drama)">Full House</a></i>, which drew solid viewership ratings nationwide throughout its run with a peak viewer rating of 42.7 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-multiple_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-multiple-6">[6]</a></sup> The series was broadcast in various parts of <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, garnering much popularity and establishing Rain as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hallyu" title="Hallyu">Hallyu</a> star. His performance in the drama won him the Best Actor award at the <a href="/wiki/KBS_Drama_Awards" title="KBS Drama Awards">KBS Drama Awards</a>. Rain next starred in <i><a href="/wiki/A_Love_to_Kill" title="A Love to Kill">A Love to Kill</a></i> opposite <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shin_Min-ah" title="Shin Min-ah">Shin Min-ah</a>.</p>
<p>In 2006, Rain made his big-screen debut in romantic comedy film <i><a href="/wiki/I%27m_a_Cyborg,_But_That%27s_OK" title="I'm a Cyborg, But That's OK">I'm a Cyborg, But That's OK</a></i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Park_Chan-wook" title="Park Chan-wook">Park Chan-wook</a>. The film won the Alfred Bauer Award at the 57th <a href="/wiki/Berlin_International_Film_Festival" title="Berlin International Film Festival">Berlin International Film Festival</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> and was selected as the opening film for the <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_International_Film_Festival" title="Hong Kong International Film Festival">Hong Kong International Film Festival</a>. Rain was nominated for and won the Best New Actor award at the 43rd Baeksang Arts Awards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="2008–2013:_Hollywood_ventures"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2008.E2.80.932013:_Hollywood_ventures">2008–2013: Hollywood ventures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 2008–2013: Hollywood ventures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2008, he starred in his first American film, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wachowskis" title="Wachowskis">Wachowskis</a>-directed <i><a href="/wiki/Speed_Racer_(film)" title="Speed Racer (film)">Speed Racer</a></i>, where he played Racer Taejo Togokahn. He then made his starring role debut in <i><a href="/wiki/Ninja_Assassin" title="Ninja Assassin">Ninja Assassin</a></i> (2009), as the main character Raizo. <i>Ninja Assassin</i> was directed by <a href="/wiki/James_McTeigue" title="James McTeigue">James McTeigue</a>, and produced by <a href="/wiki/Joel_Silver" title="Joel Silver">Joel Silver</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wachowskis" title="Wachowskis">Wachowskis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rain_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-rain-50">[50]</a></sup> The project was inspired by the ninja scenes featured from <i>Speed Racer</i>, in which Rain had impressed the Wachowskis with his portrayal as a fighter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> With <i>Ninja Assassin</i>, Rain became the first Korean-born actor to play a main character in a Hollywood movie. He won the <a href="/wiki/2010_MTV_Movie_Awards#Biggest_Badass_Star" title="2010 MTV Movie Awards">Biggest Badass award</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2010_MTV_Movie_Awards" title="2010 MTV Movie Awards">2010 MTV Movie Awards</a> for his performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, Rain returned to the small screen after 5 years with <a href="/wiki/Korean_Broadcasting_System" title="Korean Broadcasting System">KBS</a> action drama <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fugitive:_Plan_B" title="The Fugitive: Plan B">The Fugitive: Plan B</a></i>, in which he plays a young, rich and cunning Korean private investigator. At a press conference for <i>The Fugitive: Plan B</i> on September 27, 2010, Rain stated that he decided to hold off on his military service until 2011 to study for his master's degree.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> This was followed by a leading role in the aviation film <i><a href="/wiki/R2B:_Return_to_Base" title="R2B: Return to Base">R2B: Return to Base</a></i>, which was released in August 2012 to much fanfare. Rain made a surprise appearance at a special event for the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013, it was announced that Rain would appear alongside <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Willis" title="Bruce Willis">Bruce Willis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jason_Patric" title="Jason Patric">Jason Patric</a>, and <a href="/wiki/John_Cusack" title="John Cusack">John Cusack</a> in the film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Prince_(2014_film)" title="The Prince (2014 film)">The Prince</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Filming for the movie took place in the United States as well as <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The film premiered in select theaters in 2014, and was also released as video on demand.</p>
<h3><span id="2014–2016:_Success_in_China"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2014.E2.80.932016:_Success_in_China">2014–2016: Success in China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 2014–2016: Success in China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Rain made his small-screen comeback after four years in <a href="/wiki/Seoul_Broadcasting_System" title="Seoul Broadcasting System">SBS</a>'s musical drama <i><a href="/wiki/My_Lovely_Girl" title="My Lovely Girl">My Lovely Girl</a></i> (2014), opposite <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Krystal_(singer)" title="Krystal (singer)">Krystal</a> of <a href="/wiki/F(x)_(band)" title="F(x) (band)">f(x)</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> He also starred in a <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a> <a href="/wiki/Romance_film" title="Romance film">romantic</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/For_Love_or_Money_(2014_film)" title="For Love or Money (2014 film)">For Love or Money</a></i> with <a href="/wiki/Liu_Yifei" title="Liu Yifei">Liu Yifei</a>. The film, which is Rain's Chinese film debut, premiered in November 2014.</p>
<p>In December 2014, Rain started filming for his first Chinese drama <i><a href="/wiki/Diamond_Lover" title="Diamond Lover">Diamond Lover</a></i>, co-starring <a href="/wiki/Tiffany_Tang" title="Tiffany Tang">Tiffany Tang</a>. Besides the Chinese cities Shanghai and Nanjing, filming for the drama also took place in Belgium and Korea. Due to his popularity, it is said that Rain received nearly US$5.4 million for his role in <i>Diamond Lover</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The drama premiered in July 2015 and achieved huge success, earning high ratings throughout its 24-episode run.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rain next starred in the <a href="/wiki/Seoul_Broadcasting_System" title="Seoul Broadcasting System">SBS</a> drama <i><a href="/wiki/Please_Come_Back,_Mister" title="Please Come Back, Mister">Please Come Back, Mister</a></i>, which began airing in February 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> On May 2016, Rain is cast alongside <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Song" title="Victoria Song">Victoria Song</a> in the Chinese drama <i>Endless August</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2017-present:_Comeback">2017-present: Comeback</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: 2017-present: Comeback">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In March 2017, Rain was cast in the movie <i><a href="/wiki/Uhm_Bok-dong_(film)" title="Uhm Bok-dong (film)">Uhm Bok-dong</a></i> based on a true story that took place during the Japanese colonial rule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> He will star as the real-life cyclist hero <a href="/wiki/Uhm_Bok-dong" title="Uhm Bok-dong">Uhm Bok-dong</a> alongside <a href="/wiki/Kang_So-ra" title="Kang So-ra">Kang So-ra</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Artistry_and_image">Artistry and image</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Artistry and image">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:KoreAm_June_2007_cover.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="977" data-file-width="740" height="290" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/KoreAm_June_2007_cover.jpg/220px-KoreAm_June_2007_cover.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/KoreAm_June_2007_cover.jpg/330px-KoreAm_June_2007_cover.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/KoreAm_June_2007_cover.jpg/440px-KoreAm_June_2007_cover.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

Rain on the cover of <a href="/wiki/KoreAm" title="KoreAm">KoreAm</a> June 2007 issue</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id="Styles,_lyrics_and_themes"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Styles.2C_lyrics_and_themes">Styles, lyrics and themes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Styles, lyrics and themes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Since his debut, Rain has primarily been influenced by <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a> with "Bad Guy" and "How to Avoid the Sun" being categorized as the former while "Cassiopeia" and "Lack of Space" are closer to the latter. By the release of <i>It's Raining</i>, Rain, along with <a href="/wiki/Park_Jin-young" title="Park Jin-young">Park Jin-young</a>, began incorporating <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a> into his sound beginning with the title track.</p>
<p>Early in his career, most of Rain's material was handled by JYP for many years along with other songwriters and sometimes, Rain. After departing <a href="/wiki/JYP_Entertainment" title="JYP Entertainment">JYP Entertainment</a>, Rain began writing more of his material with other songwriters on <a href="/wiki/J._Tune_Entertainment" title="J. Tune Entertainment">J. Tune Entertainment</a>. Thematically, many of Rain's songs deal with the subjects of love and heartbreak in the case of "I Do" and "Love Story." On some occasions, it can be personal ("Can't Get Used to It", "My Way"), hedonistic ("Rainism", "Touch Ya"), or celebratory ("Hip Song", "Free Way").</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Voice_type">Voice type</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Voice type">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Rain's vocal range can be classified in the <a href="/wiki/Tenor" title="Tenor">tenor</a> range. His voice can be described as smooth yet husky <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> in songs such as "Love Story", "Love Song", "Nan" and "I Do." Having been influenced by American R&amp;B, he uses both <a href="/wiki/Vibrato" title="Vibrato">vibrato</a> and <a href="/wiki/Falsetto" title="Falsetto">falsetto</a> in many of his songs as well as incorporating <a href="/wiki/Rapping" title="Rapping">rapping</a> into songs like "What's Love." Rain maintains strong stance against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lipsync" title="Lipsync">lipsyncing</a> during his live performances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences">Influences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Influences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In terms of singing and dancing, Rain has been influenced by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Usher_(entertainer)" title="Usher (entertainer)">Usher</a> and <a href="/wiki/Justin_Timberlake" title="Justin Timberlake">Justin Timberlake</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Image">Image</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Image">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Rain is considered a 'world star' due to his popularity, not only in <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, but throughout <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> with fans in countries like <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. Much of his popularity is attributed to his various acting roles (varying from television like <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Full_House_(2004_TV_series)" title="Full House (2004 TV series)">Full House</a></i> to indie films like <i><a href="/wiki/I%27m_a_Cyborg,_But_That%27s_OK" title="I'm a Cyborg, But That's OK">I'm a Cyborg, But That's OK</a></i> to blockbusters like <i><a href="/wiki/Ninja_Assassin" title="Ninja Assassin">Ninja Assassin</a></i>). Before landing his role in <i><a href="/wiki/Speed_Racer" title="Speed Racer">Speed Racer</a></i>, he had expressed the desire to expand beyond the Asian market when he stated in an interview, "The reason I am active in Japan, Hong Kong, China and around Asia is that I want to succeed here and then go even more international...I would really like to see, is a top Asian artist emerge strongly from the Asian market, and then go on to succeed in the U.S. market."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rain's appeal to all demographics has made him one of Korea's highest paid celebrities by endorsers with an asking price of $1 – 1.5 million USD per endorsement. Over the years, he endorsed brands such as <a href="/wiki/Hyundai" title="Hyundai">Hyundai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lotte_(conglomerate)" title="Lotte (conglomerate)">Lotte</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KB_Card" title="KB Card">KB Card</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pizza_Hut" title="Pizza Hut">Pizza Hut</a>, Thailand dairy company <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Mill" title="Dutch Mill">Dutch Mill</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Chinese pastry Fu Mu Cakes, <a href="/wiki/Pantech" title="Pantech">Pantech</a>, <a href="/wiki/LG_Electronics" title="LG Electronics">LG Electronics</a>, <a href="/wiki/SK_Telecom" title="SK Telecom">SK Telecom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Rain has even done songs to tie-in with endorsement deals. "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Still_Believe" title="Still Believe">Still Believe</a>" was used as both an ad and a music video for <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMW</a> Korea's "Meet the Truth" campaign with appearances by Rain as well as <a href="/wiki/Park_Jin-young" title="Park Jin-young">JYP</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> "Memory in My Hand" and "Any Dream" were used in campaigns for <a href="/wiki/Pantech" title="Pantech">Pantech</a> and <a href="/wiki/Samsung" title="Samsung">Samsung</a>, respectively, in China.</p>
<p>With his booming popularity throughout the world, he has been deemed a "cultural ambassador" as he has represented South Korea in inter-Asian musical events and has appeared in a <a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a> published textbook.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_activities">Other activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Other activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Six_to_Five">Six to Five</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Six to Five">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Six to Five was Rain's first clothing line, since it also was his dream to become a fashion designer. It was launched on December 23, 2008 and was followed by a "fashion show–launch party–mini-concert" to introduce "<i>Six to Five</i>". Many stars came to support him, such as <a href="/wiki/Lee_Hyori" title="Lee Hyori">Lee Hyori</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kim_Sun-a" title="Kim Sun-a">Kim Sun-a</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chae_Rim" title="Chae Rim">Chae Rim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Girls%27_Generation" title="Girls' Generation">Girls' Generation</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Seohyun" title="Seohyun">Seohyun</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> He designed and modeled for the clothing. The label "<i>Six To Five</i>" is described by Rain as the idea of having an extra sense (i.e. from five senses to six). This label name also is said to represent his birth date, 6/25. The line was discontinued and the online mall closed by the end of 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="J._Tune_Entertainment">J. Tune Entertainment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: J. Tune Entertainment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In November 2007, Rain told the Korean media that he had left JYP Entertainment and started his own entertainment company, J. Tune Entertainment (formerly known as Rainy Entertainment). He was scheduled to be <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CEO" title="CEO">CEO</a> of the company, but told the media that he still kept in touch with his mentor and long-time trainer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Park_Jin_Young" title="Park Jin Young">Park Jin Young</a>. J. Tune Entertainment's subsidiary, J. Tune Camp debuted <a href="/wiki/MBLAQ" title="MBLAQ">MBLAQ</a>, an all-boy group, in October 2009. Rain actively participates in MBLAQ's music, either composing, writing, producing or choreographing dance routines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2010, Park Jin-Young announced that J. Tune Entertainment would be merged with <a href="/wiki/JYP_Entertainment" title="JYP Entertainment">JYP Entertainment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> It has become the largest shareholder in J. Tune Entertainment, and it is viewed as a strategic alliance between the two companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="R.A.I.N._Company">R.A.I.N. Company</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: R.A.I.N. Company">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On September 7, 2015, Rain announced through his Facebook page that he had decided to not renew his contract with <a href="/wiki/Cube_Entertainment" title="Cube Entertainment">Cube Entertainment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allkpop.com_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-allkpop.com-40">[40]</a></sup> After much speculation due to his departure from Cube,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-41">[41]</a></sup> Rain's official website announced he had created his own one-man agency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Korean_Times_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_Korean_Times-42">[42]</a></sup> In setting up the agency on a U.S.-based system, his Chinese activities will be managed by H Entertainment and Jason Jang<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> while his American agency will still be WME. His music activities will be handled by longtime manager Kim Yong Bae while his acting venture will handled by Park Jong Sun. In the near future, the agency will focus on finding talented rookies and recruiting stars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Humanitarian_work">Humanitarian work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Humanitarian work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From 2005 to 2007, Rain donated money to have 50 drinking water wells and playgrounds built in <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a>. He began taking up causes related to children by participating in the Love Photography Exhibition to help find adoptive parents for children in government care, donating a percent of his 2006 and 2007 World Tour concert proceeds to children orphaned by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AIDS" title="AIDS">AIDS</a> and participating in the Green Ribbon Hope Walking Campaign to raise funds for prevention and to help find missing children. Due to his work, he was appointed World Vision HIV/AIDS Ambassador.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> In recent years, Rain has been an advocate for environmental protection going as far as to volunteer in the Taean oil spill cleanup and donate 300 million won for clean water and clothing for the residents in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> In 2009, Rain was involved with <a href="/wiki/MTV_EXIT" title="MTV EXIT">MTV EXIT</a>, a campaign against human trafficking in Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Over the years, he has performed at concerts for various charitable causes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_issues">Legal issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Legal issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On his World 2007 tour, his scheduled concerts in <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a> were cancelled, followed by the last concert in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>. The last event at the <a href="/wiki/Staples_Center" title="Staples Center">Staples Center</a> was canceled only two hours prior to opening: Rain's producer blamed the situation on financial problems of the local promoter, while the local promoter blamed Wellmade STAR M calling them too "incompetent to handle the situation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>On March 19, 2009, a federal jury in Honolulu found that Rain, his former management agency JYP Entertainment, and two other promotion companies were guilty of breaching a contract and defrauding <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Honolulu,_Hawaii" title="Honolulu, Hawaii">Honolulu</a> promoter Click Entertainment for $2 million (originally just over $1 million) after the Hawaii concert was canceled and the promoters were not refunded the $500,000 licensing fee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-legal_suit_filed_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-legal_suit_filed-89">[89]</a></sup> Rain and JYP were ordered to pay $2.4 million each in punitive damages, $1 million for damages related to the fraud, and $2.3 million for breach of contract.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-legal_suit_award_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-legal_suit_award-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>A separate lawsuit filed by promoters Wellmade STAR M was dismissed by a South Korean court on January 28, 2010. Judge Bae Kwang-Kuk ruled in favor of Rain and blamed the plaintiff for poor preparations surrounding the cancelled U.S. tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2010, Rain and other J. Tune Creative shareholders were accused of embezzling money from the company by a fabric manufacturing company. The company claimed they suffered financial losses. Rain and the shareholders were acquitted of the charges in December of that year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> He was re investigated in April 2011 after a discrepancy was found, but was later acquitted again in June 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rain_(entertainer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Rain fulfilled his mandatory military service from October 2011 until July 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> In January 2013, Rain confirmed that he was dating actress <a href="/wiki/Kim_Tae-hee" title="Kim Tae-hee">Kim Tae-hee</a>, which then caused an investigation into whether his dating had broken military rules during his mandatory military service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rain and Kim were married on January 19, 2017 after five years of dating. He became a baptized Catholic in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> On May 23, it was announced by Kim's agency Lua Entertainment that she is currently 15 weeks pregnant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>

<li>"I'm Ready"</li>
</ul>
</div>
